< text>
I am heartbroken and devastated for my  two year old due to our experience this past Saturday at Build a Bear. üòî

We took my newly 2 year old to the Build-A-Bear location at the TO mall to finally give up his pacifier and put it in his very first bear. We had talked up the visit to him all day long and he was over the moon excited. I had checked the website prior to our visit to see what their new policies were for COVID and no where on the website does it state anything about a 2 year old having to wear a mask. Upon arrival to the store we were asked how old my son was, I had said he was newly 2 and they let me know that my child will need to wear a mask for his entire time spent in the store. I let her know he unfortunately doesn‚Äôt wear a mask for very long as it‚Äôs not required of him anywhere else (the cdc recommendation is 3 and up) so he doesn‚Äôt exactly grasp the concept yet. They told me he must wear it or be asked to leave. My son wore his mask for about 10/15 minutes and then was done wearing it. I sat on my knees so I was eye level with him and explained he was doing such a great job and that we were almost finished and he needed to keep it on until then. While I‚Äôm engaging in conversation with my son, the manager of the store screams at us from the other side of the store that if my son wont put his mask on then we needed to get out. My son screamed ‚Äúno thank you‚Äù between tears and threw his head back and hit it on the floor. I scooped him up and rocked him while he was crying and the manager again told me I needed to exit the store right now. At that point I was completely embarrassed and my child was heartbroken as he didn‚Äôt understand what was happening at all. I am completely disgusted with the way we were treated at this location and their lack of compassion and empathy towards a two year old. I don‚Äôt believe people like that should be working with children at all.

My husband who felt like my son shouldn‚Äôt be punished simply because he didn‚Äôt understand what was happening, stood in line to complete the process and have our sons bear made. The associate operating the stuffing machine watched the entire altercation happen and was in no rush to fill the bear and help get my husband out of the store. She slowly went through the whole process and had the audacity to tell my husband to hug the heart and tell her how much he loves the bear. I‚Äôm absolutely blown away by the entire experience and will never be back.

EDIT: we are not in any way anti-maskers, I am fully vaccinated and my husband and I both had our masks on the entire time. We were in no way disrespectful to anyone around us and happy to comply.< /text>

<rating>3<//rating>< review>
Build-a-Bear Workshop is a wonderfully fun store to visit at the Thousand Oaks mall. I visited the store around 5:30pm on a Friday and there was only 1 employee at the cash registers and 1 employee stuffing the animals. This would have been fine if the store wasn't packed with people. I literally had to wait 20-25 minutes to get my 1 year olds birthday bear stuffed. Thankfully I was there with my husband and I could walk around the store with him while we waited. The store itself is very clean and they have a lot of stuffed animal choices. They also have a very large selection of fun accessories for the stuffed animals. However, you could easily spend $50-80 for a stuffed animal with clothes and some accessories. Overall cute store and idea, but a bit pricey.<//review>

Really enjoyed this place. We were picking out donuts for breakfast prior to going bowling down the street, they have a deal of buy 8 get 2 free. We made our choices and then I saw the apple fritters, I had to have 2 of those, that took us up to 12 donuts and when you buy 12 donuts, you get 3 free, so we ended up leaving with 15 donuts. We will make a trip back there again.<//Text>
